Russian and French Commentary 15

Moscow: Political figures here have declared that the appointment of former Japanese Foreign Minister Koki Hirota to form a cabinet is a sign that the country is willing to adopt a moderate policy. It is said that Hirota served as the Japanese Ambassador to Russia from 1931 to 1933, and was already known at the time. He was later transferred to become the Foreign Minister in the Okada Cabinet, and he and the late Finance Minister Takahashi Korekiyo strongly opposed the large budget proposed by the military. Although his promotion to Foreign Minister was on the recommendation of former Army Minister General Araki, and he has not suffered any harm during the recent Tokyo incidents, these two points show that Hirota has a friendly relationship with the military. However, after he takes office, his measures will not worsen relations between Japan and Russia. This is what everyone believes. In addition, after Communist Party General Secretary Stalin made a statement to the President of the Associated Press, Howard, yesterday regarding the possibility of Japanese aggression against Mongolia, a deep impression has been made here. The government newspaper Izvestia published an editorial today to ease this impression, saying, "The Japanese have always been known for their straightforwardness. It is hoped that Stalin's straightforward attitude will be recognized by Japan." The attitude adopted by the Soviet Union can be seen in the Izvestia editorial. In political circles, it is believed that the announcement of the appointment of former Foreign Minister Hirota to form a cabinet, after Stalin made the above statement and the Japanese Ambassador to Russia, Ota, visited Foreign Commissioner Litvinov, is enough to ease the mood of Soviet people. (Havas telegram, 6th)

Paris: Foreign Ministry officials have declared that the appointment of former Foreign Minister Hirota to form a cabinet in Japan has been generally welcomed here. Hirota's foreign policy, especially his policy towards Russia, has always been known for its moderation, which is well known to Europeans. Recently, Hirota negotiated with the Soviet Union to organize a joint Russo-Manchukuo supervisory committee to resolve border issues between Russia and Manchukuo, which is one example. However, the situation in Tokyo is still chaotic, and it is not possible to make a hasty judgment on the future of the political situation. Political figures believe that after the recent incidents in Tokyo, many important leaders of the military have resigned (referring to Military Councilor General Masaki, General Hayashi, General Abe, General Araki, Commander of the Kwantung Army General Minami, former Army Minister General Kawashima, etc., who have been placed on the reserve list). This may intensify the opposition of the military, making it more difficult for Hirota to form a cabinet. (Havas telegram, 6th)

The United States Purchases Silver from Canada; Silver Faction Has Conflicting Opinions; Pittman Expresses Satisfaction 17

Washington: Senate silver faction senators have conflicting opinions regarding the value of the Treasury Department's policy of purchasing newly mined silver from North and South America. Senator Pittman, leader of the silver moderates, stated that the new policy is very satisfactory. Senator Thomas, leader of the inflationists, expressed the opposite view, believing that there is no benefit in buying silver without minting silver coins, as this is no different from storing zinc in the Treasury. Some sources predict that the Treasury may withdraw from world markets, but it was learned from responsible sources today that the Treasury intends to continue purchasing some silver from the world market. (National Telegram, 6th)

New York: The New York Commercial Daily reported today that the US Treasury Department's contact with the Bank of Canada to purchase newly mined Canadian silver is another move against speculators. Previously, US companies could sell newly mined Canadian silver directly to the US Treasury Department if they had the appropriate certificates. The current new law prohibits speculators from engaging in this trade. Treasury officials have previously explained that this move is very consistent with Treasury policy. In addition, the Treasury Department has also entrusted Mexican banks to purchase Mexican silver for the US. (National Telegram, 6th)

US Senator Proposes That the Government Establish a Department of Territories; The Status of the Philippines Becomes a Question 18

Washington: Senator Gibson proposed today the establishment of a Department of Territories, with a cabinet member serving as minister. The Senate is likely to consider this matter on Monday. At the same time, he announced a plan to build territorial radio stations to arouse public interest in territorial issues. Because the status of the Philippines has not yet been determined, some people question whether the island will belong to the department. However, since the law stipulates that genuine independence will be granted to the Philippines in 1946, there is no doubt that the Philippines will be subject to the department's control before independence. As for the affairs of Hawaii, Alaska, Puerto Rico, Guam, Midway Island, and the Virgin Islands, they will all be handled by the department. In addition, small islands in the Pacific such as Wake Island, Palmyra Island, Howland Island, Jarvis Island, and Baker Island will also be under the department's jurisdiction. The only territory outside the United States that is not subject to the department's control is the Panama Canal Zone. Currently, the various territories are under the jurisdiction of various government departments. The Philippines belongs to the Bureau of Insular Affairs of the War Department. Hawaii, Alaska, and Puerto Rico are under the jurisdiction of the Department of the Interior. Guam, Samoa, Midway Island, and other Pacific islands are under the control of the Navy Department. According to confirmed information this afternoon, the territorial radio station will begin broadcasting at 5:00 PM to 5:38 PM on March 11. Regarding the program, the responsible parties have contacted radio stations in Hawaii and Alaska. In addition to Gibson, Senators King and Trammell will also speak. (National Telegram, 6th)

Current Commentary

The Collection of Inheritance Tax 21

— Yu

Our country's finances have temporarily gained a respite due to the implementation of the new public debt plan, but in order to seek a fundamental solution, in addition to improving political and economic conditions, it is necessary to rectify the current tax system. The government has recently been preparing to introduce an inheritance tax. The draft prepared by the Ministry of Finance has been completed and can be implemented after it is approved by the Central Political Council and the legislative procedures are completed.

Inheritance tax, which taxes inherited property, is the fairest, most reasonable, and most modern good tax. Although financial scholars initially regarded this as a registration of the state collecting handling fees when transferring property, it is now generally recognized as an accidental and unearned income tax that is not based on personal effort. This tax is levied after inheritance and has nothing to do with the labor of the deceased.

There are two methods of levying inheritance tax: one is to tax the total amount of the estate, which has the nature of a property tax; the other is to tax the inheritance share, which is purely an unearned accidental income tax. Of the inheritance tax systems in various countries around the world, Japan only adopts the latter, while the UK has both. In the United States, the former is a federal tax and the latter is a state tax. Germany had an inheritance tax on the total amount of the estate in 1919, but after 1922, the former was included in the latter.

Our government advocated inheritance tax very early on. The National Financial Conferences in 1929 and 1934 both had resolutions on inheritance tax, but it was not implemented due to too many obstacles. Now that the Ministry of Finance has a further concrete plan, it should be able to break through the past inaction and introduce this new tax in the near future. We would like to advise the government on this matter: The progressive tax rate should not be too low, so as not to lose the meaning of regulating the national economy. The investigation and evaluation work must be fair and accurate in order to prevent abuses. If the financial authorities can pay attention to the above two points, then the inheritance tax can be promoted to its full potential.

He Jian said that after the search and suppression of the bandits in the Pingliu area of Hunan, the remnants are hiding in the Tonggu area of Jiangxi. The bandits have fewer than 400 guns. No matter how elusive their movements are, it will not be difficult to eliminate them. As for the problem of clearing up the remnants of bandits in the area bordering western Hunan and western Hubei, it is not intended to be discussed at this meeting. When Xiao He was entrenched in western Hunan, his strength was more than 20,000. After several painful suppressions by our army, more than half of them have been wiped out. After fleeing to Guizhou, they have suffered repeated defeats. Now there are only less than 10,000 people left, wandering in the areas bordering Sichuan, Guizhou, and Yunnan. The bandits are attempting to join forces with Zhu and Mao. There are two points to pay attention to in the bandits' recent actions: They take advantage of the situation to flee, without a fixed direction, making it difficult for our army to intercept them. They specialize in barren land, changing their previous actions of destroying fertile land. Their actions are swift, traveling one or two hundred miles in one night, making it difficult for the army to pursue them. Recently, a telegram was received from the front, saying that there has been heavy snow in the Sichuan-Guizhou border area for days, so there has been no major contact. I will stay in Hankou for one or two days and then return to Hunan. (Central News Agency telegram, 7th)

Tianjin Shipping Industry Association Investigates Freezing Losses, Actively Handles Aftermath, Ice in North and South Ports Melts 30

Tianjin: The Tianjin Shipping Industry Association is currently investigating the losses suffered by shipping merchants due to the freezing of Dagukou over the past two months, in order to handle the aftermath. According to Wang Gengsan, a standing committee member, the losses to shipping merchants due to the closure of Dagukou Port are at least five to six million yuan. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 7th)

Tianjin: On the 7th, the northwest wind was very strong, and much of the ice at Tanggu and Dagukou has been blown out to sea. The ice near Heigukou and the north and south ports has all melted. The Tianxing icebreaker and the Haihe Engineering Bureau went to break the ice, rescuing stranded ships. The Yijin Maru, Shunli Chunli, and three other ships had not returned by the evening. On the morning of the 7th, four ships, including the Chinese and Japanese merchant ships Changjiang Maru and Zhenjiang, arrived at Tanggu from Yantai, Dalian, and Shanghai. They passed through the harbor entrance without being blocked. The four ships were fully loaded with passengers. Passengers from the Beining and Donglai trains disembarked at Tanggu, causing great congestion. (Special dispatch on the 7th)

Tianjin: The sea route at Dagukou has been frozen for a total of fifty days. The import and export trade of various ports in North China has been severely affected. A total of 5,822 tons of goods were imported, a decrease of more than threefold compared to 18,700 tons last month. The loss of customs duties is significant. (Special dispatch on the 7th)

Tianjin: The Yongheng of the Tianjin Shipping Company arrived in Tianjin on the 7th. The ship was trapped outside the port for thirty-nine days and was severely damaged. The crew's hair was long and unkempt, and they were all exhausted from hunger. From the 6th onwards, the goods from the stranded ships entering Tanggu and Tianjin from outside the port were damaged or rotten due to freezing or water leakage in the cabins. The total losses are still difficult to estimate. The crew members of each ship also looked gaunt and emaciated and need a long period of rest to recover their strength. (Special dispatch on the 7th)

Tianjin: According to customs investigation, Dagukou was frozen for more than fifty days. In February, only eight ships entered the port and seven ships left the port. The pilots and foreign customs officers had little to do, and no taxes were collected. (Special dispatch on the 7th)

Tianjin: The Beining Railway has recently been operating poorly, with daily revenue of only 40,000 yuan. Weng Wenhao lectured on "China's Underground Resources and National Power," stating that China's underground resources are extremely rich, such as coal, iron, antimony, tungsten, and petroleum, all of which are extremely valuable treasures in terms of politics and national defense. Unfortunately, they have not been fully developed. Mr. Weng explained the output, consumption, and reserves of important minerals such as copper, tungsten, and petroleum in various countries and China in great detail using statistical data. He concluded that modern countries attach great importance to the above-mentioned minerals. If a country wants to develop its power, it must develop its underground resources. Ministry of Finance Rejects Petition from the Silverware Industry 53

Nanjing: The Beijing Silverware Industry Association united with the industry associations of various provinces and cities and sent representatives to petition the Ministry of Finance to revise the regulations on the management of silver used in silverware, in order to maintain their livelihoods. The Ministry of Finance replied on the 7th: The Ministry's regulations on the management of silver used in silverware are to control the use of silver, reduce the raw material cost of silverware, and promote the improvement of handicraft technology. In implementing the government's entire policy, it implies maintaining the industry's intentions. As for the regulations, the admixture of pure silver shall not exceed 30%. The Ministry has conducted detailed research and ordered the Central Mint to produce a variety of alloy materials for use. Handicraft technology is not hindered. You should still follow the previous approval and purchase and use it conscientiously. It is reported that the silverware industry will send members to Shanghai in the coming days to discuss everything. (Special dispatch on the 7th)

Why Mussolini Wants War 61

— Written by Loius Fisher, Translated by Bin Fu

——Observation of the European Situation under the Cloud of Killing Intent (Part 1)

Mussolini deeply believes in the supreme authority of war. "Fascism," he wrote in 1932, "never believes that permanent peace is possible or hopeful. Why? Because only war can maximize all the powers of mankind. It adds a solemn crown to those countries that can openly fight. No other attempt can be compared with war."

On December 11, 1925, Mussolini told the House of Representatives: "I regard the Italian nation as being in a state of war forever. I have said, and I will repeatedly say, that the next five or ten years are the critical juncture that will determine the fate of our country. Why are these years a critical juncture? Because the international struggle has already begun. It will become more acute with the advancement of the times. We will appear on the world stage with all our strength and will not lag behind." Amidst thunderous applause, he continued: "As for me, I live for war, for adventure, for desperate efforts." This is Mussolini's loyal warning to Europe. Of course, no one listened to him.

For fear that anyone would still have doubts about his ambitions, he reiterated them on December 11, 1925. "The fundamental obligation of Fascist Italy," he said, "is to replenish its armaments on land, sea, and air. We must be able to mobilize five million people. We must strengthen our fleet. Our air force must be strengthened until its rattling machine sound overwhelms all the noisy sounds on the peninsula, and its wings darken the boundless sky. In this way, between 1935 and 1940, when a tragic scene occurs in European history, we can make our voices loud. We will make our authority recognized by the world. But this, of course, requires several years of preparation." Mussolini is truly a great and active figure. He is also the most frank politician in Europe. As a Roman daily, Ottobre, always reveals on its masthead: "Mussolini is always right." And now, we are precisely in "between 1935 and 1936."

Mussolini's attempt is to conquer foreign countries. Personal ambition, personal pride, and the politician's view of his historical mission have shaped his policies. Mussolini considers himself to be the modern Caesar, dreaming of a new Roman Empire. Rome is an eternally beautiful city. Mussolini has spent a lot of effort in repairing Roman monuments. As soon as I arrived in Rome, I went to the great Palazzo Venezia. It was made of stones moved from the ancient Roman Colosseum. It used to be the Pope's private property and is now Mussolini's headquarters. From here, there is a wide Imperial Avenue, with Trajan's Forum and columns on one side, and the Roman Forum on the other, leading all the way to the solemn and great Colosseum. Before the Roman Forum, there is a brick wall, on which Mussolini inlaid four large marble maps. The first map is Europe, the upper part of Africa, and the Near East, made of pure black and shiny marble, with green stripes around the sea, and the city of Rome is marked with a circle of coffee color. It shows the situation at the beginning of the founding of Rome in the eighth century BC. The second map represents the Roman Empire in 146 BC. The coffee-colored circle has expanded to include half of Spain, Corsica, Sardinia, Italy, the Illyrian coast—present-day Yugoslavia—Macedonia, Thrace, and Carthage. This is the situation after the Punic Wars. In 14 AD, as shown in the third map, Rome controlled all of Spain and France, Germany south of the Rhine, southern Europe bounded by the Danube, Constantinople and its hinterland, Asia Minor, Cilicia, Antioch, Syria, Palestine, Egypt south to Sudan, Libya, all of Carthage, and part of Numidia. Trajan (98-117-A.D.) developed the empire to its highest peak. His borders, in addition to the past coffee-colored entirety, also included Britain, Germany (as far as the Baltic Sea), the Balkans (almost to Russia), Cappadocia, Armenia (to the entire Caspian Sea), Mesopotamia (down to the Persian Gulf), and Arabia. Mussolini is of course paying attention to that fourth map. His Roman ancestors conquered Britain before they wanted to occupy Abyssinia. Now, Mussolini wants to reverse that precedent.

Reason tells us that there is no room on that brick wall to accommodate another map. But Fascism is still trying its best to impress the psychology of imperial worship into the minds of the people. "Empires are constantly rising and falling in alternation," a haughty Fascist said to me yesterday. "Can the British Empire continue to exist permanently?" This kind of argument can be heard everywhere. Five days ago, I had a long conversation with Rossoni, who can probably be regarded as the third most important figure in Italy. He said: "Some people think that the world is stable, but the driving force of history cannot be ignored. I always believe in imperialism." Mussolini himself has explained this dogma several times. In 1926, he said: "Italy demands that the great powers recognize her need for sunshine and land. If they do not recognize it, Italy will have to take decisive action."

"Africa and the East (that is, Asia Minor) are the direction of Italy's development," as Mussolini said in March 1934. He has several "apprentices" who are even more certain. They think of Abyssinia, that is certain, as well as Egypt and India. It is a fact that the Italians have tried their best to organize and seduce Indian students studying in Europe. On October 12, 1935, nine days after the start of the Abyssinian War, the Roman newspaper; Massaggero said:

Italy has simultaneously gained a very superior position in India's economic and moral foundations. All of India has united under the common feeling of hatred for the alien governors who rule them. India is willing to express respect to countries that challenge Britain. ... Britain's attempt to instigate people of color to oppose us appears to be a failure. The majority of the people in India can understand the benefits of this, that is, Italy's advancement into Africa is no different from India's resurrection... Enslaved Indians are regarding us as their last hope. The Jewish Fascist nationalists led by Jabotinsky are trying their best to advocate that Italy take over Palestine. The Italian authorities have given them encouragement. Italy has been watching Syria. Everyone knows about Rome's attempt to gain a foothold in Yemen on the Arabian Peninsula. These ambitions will have no end.

The motives behind imperialism are very inconsistent, and public opinion often changes with them. Indeed, recently a small number of scholars have proposed that imperialism is no longer caused by economic reasons. Therefore, Mussolini's policies can be said to be an unusually interesting question. If we know the source and nature of Fascist imperialism—this may have a great relationship to that chaotic world.

The Reasons for Rural Decline in China 83

President of the Agricultural College of Central University, Ji Shuwen

What I am going to say today about the reasons for rural decline only concerns the situation in China. And I will divide what I am going to say into two parts: I will summarize and discuss the opinions expressed in various journals and newspapers on this issue; and I must also express my personal views, which are somewhat different, on this topic.

I. Summarizing the general opinions on the causes of rural decline and discussing their importance.

Since China opened its doors to foreign trade, it has been shocked by the strength of other countries. Most people have focused on the development of cities, completely ignoring the countryside. Recently, they have gradually realized that cities are not the only solution, and have turned to paying attention to revitalizing the countryside. Recently, there have been countless articles in magazines and newspapers about this. Summarizing the reasons for rural decline, they generally fall into the following three categories:

External oppression is still the main reason for the decline of rural China, including the aggression of imperialist powers and the extraction of exorbitant taxes. Under the oppression of these two external forces, the countryside has no choice but to decline. First, let's talk about the aggression of imperialist powers:

Imperialism initially used force to oppress China, in addition to ceding land and demanding huge indemnities. Besides the inability to control tariffs, they were also allowed to set up factories and banks in the country. This political and economic aggression, coming from both sides, has caused China to suffer direct and indirect losses of more than tens of millions of yuan every year. Moreover, foreign goods, with the protection of the lowest tariffs and the backing of warships, can come smoothly and occupy the market directly. Even in remote rural areas, the most basic daily necessities are replaced by foreign goods. Our original Chinese handicrafts have all been defeated by foreign goods, and the prices of agricultural products have fallen below the cost of production. Farmers work from dawn to dusk, busy all year round, but only to benefit others, while they themselves suffer from cold and hunger. If you open the customs trade registers for the past hundred years, you will know that, except for the last three years, when the value of goods fell due to special reasons such as the Northeast being occupied, the value of imported goods has been increasing year by year since the beginning of the Republic of China until the 20th year of the Republic of China. The annual outflow of money has even reached 200 to 300 million yuan. What we buy are foreign goods that suppress our domestic products, and very few necessities for developing our domestic industry. Therefore, not only is the amount of trade deficit alarming, but there is also a real danger of reducing the sales of local products. The speed of rural decline has naturally accelerated!

Secondly, let's talk about the extraction of exorbitant taxes. Paying taxes is originally a duty that everyone should fulfill. However, the heavy layers of exorbitant taxes are also an important cause of rural decline. According to the investigation of the Rural Reconstruction Committee, the number of surcharges is as high as fifty or sixty in Jiangxi, more than seventy in Zhejiang, and more than one hundred and five in Jiangsu. As for the amount exceeding the regular tax, Jiangxi Province has more than twenty-five times the amount, which is not much, while Hebei Province even has more than eighty times the amount. In addition to the surcharges on land tax, there is also the "pre-collection," which was not uncommon in Sichuan during the era of the warlord Liu Xiang, who collected taxes several years in advance. Some places even collected taxes up to the 70th year of the Republic of China! In addition, there are also "requisitions" similar to land tax surcharges, which are also collected according to the amount of land or the regular tax. Although this kind of requisition is not as common as land tax surcharges, it is a common occurrence in places where transportation is inconvenient, politics are corrupt, and farmers' knowledge is limited. Moreover, this kind of requisition is often more burdensome than land tax surcharges! Not to mention the various special taxes levied on farmers in various places at any time. With the limited resources of the farmers, and the endless extraction of exorbitant taxes, how can the countryside not collapse! Now the central and local governments are trying to limit land tax surcharges and reduce various miscellaneous taxes, which is a gratifying thing, but the previous wounds are too difficult to heal.

The inherent weakness of the countryside: Unequal land distribution in China, too few self-cultivating farmers in the countryside, the inability of farm household income and expenditure to offset each other, and the inability to improve production techniques are all weaknesses inherent to the countryside, and are also the main reasons for rural decline.

First, the unequal distribution of land: According to the results of the survey, the vast majority of farmers in China only own a very small amount of land, while a very small number of landlords own the vast majority of land. Farmers who are so poor that they have no place to stand, or farmers who have land but are unable to cultivate it, have no choice but to rent land from landlords. Since they rent land from landlords, they naturally have to pay rent. As a result, they have to give at least half of their hard-earned income to the landlords, and what is left is not enough to maintain their basic living standards. Unequal land distribution has led to the complete merger of land by the powerful. This has been a historical trend since ancient times. Private land, royal land, and public land systems were all attempts to solve this problem, but none of them succeeded. Now this problem is even more urgent. How to enable tillers to own land is a topic that must be discussed.

Second, the imbalance of farm household income and expenditure: According to a recent news report, a survey of rural areas in the suburbs of Shanghai showed that in seventy-two villages in the western suburbs of Shanghai, with a total of nine hundred and forty-five households and four thousand and forty-nine people, the total income this year was 97,971 yuan and 5 jiao, while the total expenditure was 149,918 yuan and 7 fen, resulting in an annual deficit of 51,946 yuan and 2 jiao and 7 fen. The average annual deficit per household was 54 yuan, 9 jiao, 3 fen, and 2 li, and the average per person was 12 yuan, 6 jiao, 8 fen, and 8 li. This phenomenon of income and expenditure imbalance is not only the case in the western suburbs of Shanghai, but also in other places if a detailed investigation is conducted. Because farmers' lives are difficult, they naturally have to live on loans. Self-cultivating farmers also suffer from low prices of agricultural products, exploitation by exorbitant taxes, and high living standards. Their lives are also equally difficult, and they also have to rely on loans to get by.

Following borrowing is the exploitation of usury. According to a report by the League of Nations economic experts, "Usury is the greatest pain for Chinese farmers. The interest rate on Chinese farmers' loans is as low as 33%, and even as high as 100% or more." Since farmers' lives are difficult, their funds are naturally lacking, and they have to borrow to survive. This means they have to use the exploitation of usury to quench their thirst.

Third, the failure to improve production techniques: Our Chinese agriculture was originally based on a small-scale system, which is not suitable for large-scale production. Farmers' knowledge is shallow, and all agricultural techniques are based on old traditions, without improvement. At the same time, the progress of agriculture in other countries is rapid, and the improvement of agricultural products is effective. Our Chinese agriculture, however, remains stagnant, which is inevitably compared unfavorably. For example, tea is a major agricultural export of China. Thirty years ago, our export volume ranked first in the world. Recently, it has been defeated by the tea of Ceylon, Java, and India. Another example is the international silk market, which has also been occupied by the silk of Japan and Italy. Even the main food crops in the country—rice and wheat—have to be supplemented by foreign rice and wheat.

In short, due to unequal land distribution, they cannot escape the plunder of landlords; due to income and expenditure imbalance, they cannot escape the exploitation of usury; due to the failure to improve production techniques, they cannot escape the squeeze of international agricultural products. This is the inherent weakness of the countryside, and its decline is only natural.

The impact of natural disasters and man-made disasters: The decline of the rural areas in China is also greatly affected by natural and man-made disasters. For example, the flood in the 20th year of the Republic of China. According to a report by the National Relief Commission for the Great Famine of the Republic of China, in the summer and autumn of the tenth year, 29 million people and 70,000 square miles of land suffered from an unprecedented flood. The disaster area lost 900 million yuan of agricultural crops and 200 million yuan of property. According to a report by the Agricultural Society of China on the disasters in the 13th year of the Republic of China, there were droughts in 220 counties in 20 provinces, floods in 119 counties in 13 provinces, locust plagues in 28 counties in 8 provinces, and other disasters in 76 counties in 13 provinces, disease in 27 counties in 6 provinces, wind disasters in 46 counties in 11 provinces, hail disasters in 41 counties in 10 provinces, frost disasters in 20 counties in 6 provinces, and landslides in 2 counties in 2 provinces, with a total loss of more than 150,000 yuan. According to a report from the National Flood Relief Commission: last year (the 24th year of the Republic of China), the flood affected an area of 74.2 million mu in the Yangtze River basin, affecting 10 million people and causing a property loss of 22.6 million yuan; the disaster area in the Huai River basin affected an area of 80.4292 million mu, affecting 9 million people and causing a property loss of 21.825 million yuan; the total disaster area in the Yangtze River, Yellow River, and Huai River basins affected an area of 155.739319 million mu, affecting 19 million people and causing a property loss of 54.445 million yuan. What is said above is only the major disaster situations in recent years. There is no year in China where no province is unaffected by natural disasters. The direct losses are certainly great, and the various indirect losses are even more difficult to calculate. (To be continued)

Hebei-Chahar Political Affairs Committee Plans to Discuss Anti-Communist Measures, Strengthen Defense Forces in Southern Hebei, and Hebei-Chahar-Shanxi Provinces Jointly Prevent Communism 84

Beiping Correspondent: Bandit guerrillas have been discovered in Renxian, Yaoshan, and Julu in Hebei. The authorities have taken measures to suppress them. It is reported that the bandits have established a temporary organization with Renxian as the center, with March 18th as the date for a demonstration. As for Shanxi, Fenyang has not fallen. The Beiping Church has recently received a telegram from the Fenyang Church stating that the missionaries are all safe and there are no Communists in Fenyang.

After returning to Baoding, he will go to Shunde tomorrow (the 7th) to convene a meeting of county magistrates to discuss suppression measures.

Since the bandits fled to Shanxi, the military authorities here, in order to prevent the defeated bandits from invading the territory of Hebei and Chahar, as Shanxi Province borders Hebei and Chahar, in addition to having previously instructed the troops of the two provinces of Hebei and Chahar to strictly guard against them at various important locations, recently Yan Xishan, Director of the Taiyuan Pacification Headquarters, sent Yan, a member of the Headquarters, to Beiping to visit the local authorities to discuss the issue of assisting in preventing Communism. It is reported that the authorities, considering the close relationship, have agreed to provide assistance within their capabilities. The methods are being carefully planned. At the same time, the counties are instructed to reorganize the Baojia system in order to achieve unity between the military and the people and to maximize the effectiveness of Communism prevention under the principle of "three parts military and seven parts political," so that the Communist bandits cannot step into the territory of Hebei and Chahar. (6th)

The Puppet State: Restrictions on Chinese Laborers Leaving the Pass Due to Unstable Japanese Political Situation and Puppet Mongol Relations 85

Tianjin Dispatch: The border police of the puppet state at Shanhaiguan suddenly, starting from March 1st, refused entry and exit to Chinese entering or leaving the pass. Those who insisted on entering the puppet state had to purchase a special exit permit at a cost of twenty yuan per permit, sold by the Daito Company under the guise of a security deposit. If Chinese laborers could leave the puppet territory within two months of exiting the pass, they could return the permit to the Daito Company in Shanhaiguan and receive nineteen yuan back, with one yuan deducted as a handling fee. Those who failed to leave within the deadline would not be refunded. The puppet authorities did not announce this matter in advance. Before this month, with the occurrence of Mongol-puppet disputes, Shanhaiguan, Gubeikou, and Malanyu implicitly refused Chinese entry, claiming it was to prevent insurgents from infiltrating and causing trouble. However, the restrictions were still based on individual assessment, so travelers could still find ways to exit the pass, though sometimes obstructed. Now, with the promulgation of the new rule, laborers seeking a living outside the pass, besides their shoulder bag, could barely afford travel expenses. Suddenly requiring a twenty-yuan security deposit is tantamount to prohibiting entry. For days, hundreds of men and women have been stranded at Yuguan. On the second night, passengers on the through train from Beiping to Shenyang were blocked, with over three hundred people stranded, unable to advance or retreat. As a result, passenger traffic on the Beining Railway through train from Beiping to Shenyang has sharply decreased, but the trains continue to run as usual to maintain transportation. On the third day, the Beining Railway Bureau specifically issued a notice, publicly announcing the puppet state's measures to restrict Chinese from exiting the pass at Yuguan, advising travelers leaving the pass to be cautious. Those capable of paying the twenty-yuan security deposit should purchase tickets and board the train to avoid being stranded midway, unable to advance or retreat. Also, fearing that many laborers from Zhili and Shandong are ignorant and unaware of the announcement, on the fourth day, all stations were instructed to first ask passengers boarding the train for a special identity card from the puppet Daito Company before selling tickets. Those without it would be refused tickets. Recently, the Oriental Travel Agency, upon request from the Beining Railway Bureau, was tasked with negotiating with the puppet authorities to cancel this measure to avoid excessive losses for the railway. However, the manager of the Oriental Travel Agency, Zhang Yongqi, is not back from Shanghai, and the deputy manager, Hirayama, is unwilling to take responsibility, so negotiations can only take place after Zhang returns. According to the puppet authorities, this prohibition on Chinese laborers leaving the pass is specifically targeted at small vendors and laborers from Zhili and Shandong. Because every spring, laborers from inside the pass flock to the outside of the pass to seek a living, leading to an increase in unemployment within the puppet territory and a surplus of laborers, to prevent them from becoming bandits and disrupting the security of the puppet territory, the authorities decided to implement these restrictions. This measure is not intended to be long-term. However, according to other sources, the puppet's prohibition on Chinese laborers leaving the pass has two causes: The relationship between the puppet state and Mongolia remains tense. The Japanese Kwantung Army's Xiangyue Division is being transported to the Northeast, and its troops in Harbin and Qiqihar are also on the move, fearing unrest during this time. Also, due to the unsettled Japanese political situation, to prevent insurgents from entering the country and taking advantage of the situation to revolt, there is a temporary restriction on Chinese traveling there. The puppet side's plans to advance into the Mongolian-Suiyuan border area are gradually unfolding. The Tongliao-Kuping Railway is about to begin construction. The South Manchuria Railway has commissioned the Okura Corporation to undertake civil engineering work, recruiting Chinese laborers to perform arduous tasks. Okura has set up an office in Tianjin to recruit. Each time laborers are recruited, they are transported in groups of four truckloads through Gubeikou to Chifeng and Dolon. However, many laborers who left the pass to seek employment last year were deceived, ending up with nothing. Therefore, this year, although Okura offers higher wages, very few are responding, and no one is willing to go. The puppet authorities, in order to force Chinese laborers to take this route and prevent them from seeking a living outside the pass, are making it difficult with the special identity card. However, this measure does not apply to foreigners from other countries. (5th)

Southwestern Aviation Company: The Process of Contending to Operate Flights in Guangdong, and the Obstruction of China National Aviation Corporation Planes in Guangdong 86

Guangzhou Dispatch: The Sino-Vietnamese Civil Aviation (flights from within China to Hanoi, Annam, connecting with French flights to Europe), its route passes through Guangdong and Guangxi provinces. Initially, the Southwestern Aviation Company, operated by the Guangdong and Guangxi authorities, negotiated with the French government to operate the route. Later, the Ministry of Transportation of Nanjing ultimately assigned the Sino-Vietnamese route to the China National Aviation Corporation (CNAC), extending the company's Shanghai-Guangzhou route to Hanoi. It officially opened on February 13th, and a flight had already flown south. On the 27th, CNAC's "Fujian" plane arrived in Guangzhou from Shanghai, carrying a batch of Chinese and foreign mail, intending to fly to Vietnam from Guangzhou as the second flight. Due to bad weather, it temporarily parked at the Ersha Tou Airport. The Guangdong authorities, upon receiving the report, claimed that the Sino-French route was originally contracted by the Southwestern Aviation Company, and now CNAC had not obtained the approval of the Guangdong and Guangxi authorities, and that unilaterally sending planes to fly over was considered an act of infringing on public enterprises. Therefore, on the 28th, they sent people to Ersha Tou, stopping the "Fujian" from flying further, and notified the CNAC office in Guangdong, stating that CNAC planes were only allowed to operate on the Guangzhou-Shanghai route and were not allowed to extend the route to French Hanoi. They were instructed to transfer the mail carried by the "Fujian" from Shanghai to the Post Office for delivery. The office had no choice but to comply, first sending the "Fujian" back to Shanghai on the 1st of this month, reporting the obstruction in Guangdong. The right to operate the Sino-Vietnamese civil aviation route is pending negotiation between the Ministry of Transportation and the Guangdong and Guangxi authorities, it is said. (March 3rd)

Communist Bandits in Various Counties of Hebei Province Decide to Divide Areas for Suppression; The Communist Bandits in Ren County Will Be Resolved Politically; The Suppression Army Actively Begins Deploying Defenses 87

Baoding Dispatch: In order to eradicate banditry throughout Hebei Province, Hebei Chairman Song Zheyuan previously convened a meeting in Beiping with leaders of various stationed troops, including Security Director Zhang Yunrong, 63rd Army Commander Feng Zhanhai, 53rd Army Chief of Staff Wang Yatang, to discuss suppression measures. Upon investigation, in Hebei Province, apart from the Liu Guitang gang, which had already been completely annihilated some time ago, there were still over ten thousand communist bandits in the Yao Mountain and Julu area of southern Hebei's Ren County. The provincial government has already formulated separate solutions for these communist bandits, deciding to eliminate them through political means. Security Director Zhang Yunrong has also drafted a plan to suppress the communist bandits and a program to reform them, which is being submitted to the Hebei-Chahar Political Affairs Committee for review. In addition, the 29th Army has dispatched a Liu Battalion of infantry to suppress them, so as to prevent the bandit forces from expanding. In addition to the aforementioned two gangs in the province, other banditry is scattered in small groups. However, because they are scattered in various counties, they pose a threat to local disturbances at any time. Moreover, with the rise of the green gauze curtain, it is difficult for farmers and residents in various counties to live and work in peace. Song Zheyuan believes that eradicating these scattered bandit groups is also an urgent task. Furthermore, because the areas where these bandit groups are scattered are vast, they arise one after another, making it extremely difficult to eliminate them completely. It is necessary to mobilize a large number of troops simultaneously in different areas and wipe them out in one fell swoop in order to be effective. It was agreed with the leaders of various stationed troops to divide the entire province into four bandit suppression areas, with Song's 29th Army, Shang Zhen's 32nd Army, Wan Fulin's 53rd Army, and Feng Zhanhai's 63rd Army each occupying one area, and simultaneously starting to suppress them. Each army has dispatched elite troops specifically responsible for bandit suppression. After this regional bandit suppression plan was agreed upon, the armies have now begun to actively deploy their defenses separately, and it is expected that they will be completely eradicated within two months. The provincial government has also ordered the county governments to promptly report the bandit situation in their counties, so that teams can be dispatched to suppress them. At the same time, it has also ordered the county defense corps to assist the army in bandit suppression at any time. After this large-scale and painful suppression, the banditry in Hebei Province should gradually disappear. As for the communist bandits in the Yao Mountain and Julu area of Ren County, estimated to number over ten thousand, they originated from the six villages (Liu Village, Shi Village, Guo Village, Huai Village, Li Village, Luo Village) and four manors (Gan Village, Zhu Village, Feng Village, Guan Village) of Ren County. The internal organization of these bandits is quite strict, divided into foreign affairs, politics, military affairs, and other groups, with a man named Liu Wenzhong serving as the Red Army Commander-in-Chief and Commander of the Guerrilla Brigade. The so-called guerrilla team is the armed force of the bandits, consisting of thirteen guerrilla teams in total. The uniforms and equipment are very neat, and many of the firearms are new. According to investigations, these bandits have more than fifty submachine guns, over a hundred Mauser pistols, and over three hundred 38-type rifles. Last year, Zhu De and Mao Zedong provided these bandits with over twenty thousand yuan, and there were also three female students who had returned from studying in Russia, mixed in to guide everything. Recently, since the Liu Battalion of the 29th Army began suppressing them, the bandit situation is no longer as rampant as it used to be. However, these bandits gather and disperse unpredictably. Moreover, because they already have a considerable organization and have been persuaded and lured, it is necessary to start by correcting their ideology. Therefore, the provincial government is currently awaiting the Hebei-Chahar Political Affairs Committee's review of the bandit suppression plan and reform program, so as to base its actions on them, and has decided to resolve the issue with 30% military force and 70% political power. (March 5th)

He excelled in his studies. In the 21st year of the Republic (1932), after returning to China, Sichuan Chairman and Commander of the Northern Route Bandit Suppression, Liu Xiang, recruited military specialists to attract talent. The Tangkou Electric Light Factory in the 8th district of the county previously lost over two piculs of white rice due to theft. Li A'er and Li Baofa, relatives of the deceased, were sentenced to two months of imprisonment each for obstructing official duties. Zhang Wencai was sentenced to three months of imprisonment.

As a result, squad leader Yao Binghua and two team members were injured. They have already gone to the city to report to the team headquarters for investigation.

Jiangyin: Dispute over the Property of Two Consortiums Resolved 94

The Southeast Township Academy and the West Township Office of this county managed property, which the province previously ordered the county Education Bureau to take over. It repeatedly and strictly ordered the county government to urge the Education Bureau to implement the takeover. Representatives of the two groups, Mao Youru, Chen Zhongda, and others, were dissatisfied and submitted a petition to the provincial government, filing an administrative appeal. It was decided to change the decision and transfer all the school property to the Education Bureau for management. After receiving the ruling, the two groups still did not comply and filed another appeal with the Ministry of Education, which was again rejected. They continued to file a lawsuit with the Administrative Court as a final resort. At the same time, they dispatched representatives Jiang Hong and others to Beijing to visit the authorities and argue their case according to law. After over a year, it remained unresolved. Until the other day, the Executive Yuan decided to cancel the appeal decision and the original decision. The property of the two groups will be managed by the township offices and academies, with the county ordering them to select personnel to take over according to regulations.

Jiading: Military Police Damage the Shanghai-Nanjing Bus 95

On March 5th, as the former County Chief Xu left office and went to Shanghai, the entire shift of police officers from the No. 1 Branch of the Nanxiang Public Security Bureau escorted him from Xiang to Luoyang Bridge. A No. 18 bus from the Shanghai-Nanjing Company happened to be coming from Shanghai, and five military police officers stopped it and boarded to return to Xiang without buying tickets. After arriving in Xiang, stationmaster Liu Kaiyi negotiated with the police platoon leader to purchase supplementary tickets. Other military police officers suddenly used their rifle butts to smash the doors and windows of the bus, and even tried to beat the driver. After stationmaster Liu intervened, they stopped. It is reported that the Shanghai-Nanjing Company believes that this situation obstructs road operations and is negotiating with the public security authorities.

Travel Notes from Hankou to Canton (3) 97

— Zhao Junhao

(Travel Correspondence from Our Reporter) Recording the Lu River Bridge

I left Changsha for Zhuzhou on the morning of the 4th. The train I took was the Changsha-Zhuzhou-Pingxiang section, also managed by the Hunan-Hubei Railway Bureau. This route was originally only the Zhuzhou-Pingxiang section, run by merchants. Later, it was nationalized and extended from Zhuzhou to Changsha, serving as the only thoroughfare for transporting coal from Pingxiang. The passenger car I boarded was a converted wooden shed used for transporting goods, dilapidated and filthy, beyond imagination. But this was the only passenger car, and there was no other choice. After the train started, both sides were lined with shops, barbershops, teahouses, small restaurants, with everything available. At first glance, it almost seemed like traveling in an alleyway by train, which was quite amusing. It was not until outside the suburbs of Changsha that it emerged from the alleyway and headed into the open fields. As for the situation inside the car, it was similar to the Yangzhou ferry. Peddlers shouted and sold all kinds of food, with everything available, except for women singing songs. I heard someone in the car say, "This train travels very slowly. People who want to freeload can jump on, and when the ticket inspector comes, they can jump off. There are even some brave ones who cling to the bottom of the car to hitch a ride. There are iron rods between the axles at the bottom of the car, and people sit on the rods without any fear. If they lose their grip and get crushed to death, people will scold them for being useless." Alas! How pitiful. Changsha has a lot of rain. When this train travels, passengers must have umbrellas because the roof leaks. During heavy rain, they may be drenched all over. So-and-so said this, and I could not help but laugh.

Around 1 p.m., the train arrived in Zhuzhou. Zhuzhou is a small town belonging to Xiangtan, the starting point of the Zhuzhou-Shaoguan section of the Guangzhou-Hankou Railway. When the future Beijing-Hunan Railway is completed, this town will surely be a key location. However, because it is close to Changsha, it seems that there is no prospect of commercial development. After getting off the train, I immediately went to the office of the Second Subdivision of the Seventh General Section of the Zhuzhou-Shaoguan Engineering Bureau for a short rest. The place was an ancestral hall, with spacious houses, extremely rare in this remote area. The surrounding mountains overlapped, and clear water flowed around the front door, making the scenery quite pleasant. Engineer Jin Shidi and Section Chief Xie Yue of the Train Operations Section have been working here for more than two years, and life is very lonely. I smiled and said to them, "The Zhuzhou-Shaoguan section will soon be open to traffic. The mental pleasure of completing a great achievement should compensate for the loneliness of life." After stopping in Zhuzhou for two hours, I transferred to the Zhuzhou-Shaoguan Bureau's engineering vehicle to Lukou to visit the Lu River Bridge. Midway, we passed the home of General Section Chief Wu Siyuan and climbed down from the car using a ladder in front of his door. This was the first time in my life that I had gotten off a car in this way. After resting at Wu's home for half an hour, we rode in a hand-cranked car to the bank of the Lu River. Upon investigation, the most difficult projects in the Zhuzhou-Shaoguan Bureau of the Guangzhou-Hankou Railway are bridges and tunnels. The southern section has more tunnels (the southern section also has five major arch bridge projects), and the northern section has more bridges. Of the bridge projects, the construction of the Lu River, Mi River, and Lei River was more difficult. The Lu, Mi, and Lei rivers are all tributaries of the Xiang River, and are necessary routes for the railway. After I boarded the hand-cranked car, four workers drove the car like flying. The weather was cold, and the wind was strong, making it unbearably cold. I felt very bitter, but then I thought about how hard the staff on this road worked, and I was fortunate to have the opportunity to come and see it. Why should I be afraid? My spirits were lifted. After twenty minutes of driving, we arrived at the bank of the Lu River, and the majestic bridge was revealed before my eyes. After getting off the car, we crossed the river to the south bank, led by Section Chief Wu, and walked through several wooden frames to visit the tenth pier. This pier was the final project of the bridge, and there were many workers who were pouring cement into the pier. The scene was very intense. The place where I was standing was already below the river surface because to build the Lu River bridge pier, it was necessary to first build a dam to cut off the water flow. We were standing inside the dam, so we were below the river surface. The width of the Lu River surface is 300 meters between the north and south banks. When the water level is at its lowest, it is only three meters deep, but at its highest, it rises to 18 meters. The length of the Lu River Bridge is 344 meters, with a height of 21 meters (from the bridge base to the top of the pier). There are two bridge abutments (that is, the two ends of the bridge) and ten piers, totaling eleven spans. There are seven plate girder spans, each span being 18 meters long, and four truss girder spans, each span being 55 meters long. Every year, from late spring to early summer, around April and May, is the time when the Lu River floods. During this time, there is a lot of rainfall, coupled with flash floods, which often overflows the two banks, making bridge construction particularly difficult. The flood of the 23rd year of the Republic (1934) was even more severe, with more than 20 floods of various sizes. Often, overnight, the water level would rise seven or eight feet, making it impossible to predict. Therefore, the work done today would be washed away by the next morning, leaving nothing but sighs to the rushing river. In addition, the piles used for damming were mostly wooden planks due to economic constraints, with only a few steel sheet piles, and they were old goods purchased from the Yangtze River Ferry project in the capital. In the autumn of the 23rd year, just as the two sides of the steel sheet piles were installed, they were completely washed away by the flood. Thus, all the work was wasted, and we had to start again. This is the general situation of the construction difficulties of the bridge. Section Chief Wu said, "This bridge has gone through all kinds of hardships, which cannot be described in a word. Now we are working day and night. The pier project will be completed in four days. As for laying the sleepers and tracks, it will take a short time. At the latest, by early April, we can directly cross the bridge from Zhuzhou and move forward." The Mi River Bridge has already been completed, and the Lei River Bridge will be completed by early April. Therefore, the entire line will be open to traffic by the end of May without any problem. The abutment project of the Lu Bridge was contracted by Dong Ziji, and the bridge erection project was contracted by the Shanghai Xinzhong Company. I visited the bridge for a long time, and it was already night. We returned to the Seventh General Section office by hand-cranked car for a rest. The day's activities came to an end here. After dinner, I recorded this by kerosene lamp until midnight. Tomorrow morning, I will continue to take the Zhuzhou-Shaoguan Bureau's engineering vehicle to Hengshan. (Late night on March 4th in Lukou)

Business Report for the 24th Year of the Republic

The company's business report for the 24th year of the Republic stated: "Our company has only been in operation for a year and a half. Looking at the domestic and international economic and financial situation, we know that simply relying on existing resources is not enough to achieve our goals. Therefore, at the beginning of this year, we set a policy to consolidate our own foundation internally and establish a good reputation externally, in order to promote Sino-foreign cooperation and develop domestic construction. Over the past year, we have done our best. With the joint cooperation of government agencies and the financial and industrial sectors at home and abroad, we have made great contributions to various construction projects. Some have been successfully completed, while others are in the design and negotiation stage. There are still many more, and we hope to gradually realize them in the 25th year of the Republic. The final accounts for the 24th year show a total profit of 1,376,751 yuan, one jiao, and seven fen for the entire year. The total operating expenses for the year were 164,773 yuan, four jiao, and four fen. The net profit after deducting expenses was 1,211,977 yuan, seven jiao, and three fen. After deducting one-tenth for the public reserve fund, paying shareholders a regular dividend of 7%, and a bonus of 3.5%, the remaining amount will be used as retained earnings for this year. This is a general overview of the business operations over the past year, which should be gratifying to the shareholders. Now is the time of currency reform and economic recovery. Our company's reputation has been established at home and abroad. We hope that the financial and industrial sectors will continue to cooperate with the same spirit as in the past, so that domestic construction projects can progress and succeed one by one. This is our company's greatest hope for the future. Detailed figures for the final accounts for the 24th year and the profit distribution plan are detailed in separate statements, which we hope you will examine."

Statistics of Annual Business Revenue and Expenditure

The company's total net profit for the year was over 1,210,000 yuan. The asset side of the balance sheet listed: Cash 1,080,831.24 yuan, accounts receivable 528,881.55 yuan, receivables 65,105.63 yuan, advances 738,522.79 yuan, collection items 34,350.03 yuan, fixed assets 15,787.79 yuan, other 5,401.60 yuan, totaling 1,478,185.63 yuan. The liability side listed: Capital 10,000,000 yuan, public reserve fund 100,000 yuan, retained earnings 56,265.01 yuan, transferred collection 2,738,522.79 yuan, collected payments 34,351.03 yuan, accounts payable 569,500 yuan, deposit guarantee 71,235.07 yuan, totaling 13,569,873.90 yuan. The net profit after offsetting revenue and expenditure was 1,211,977.73 yuan. The income statement showed: Debit expenditures of 151,578.77 yuan, handling fee expenses of 686.38 yuan, interest expenses of 12,508.29 yuan, and net profit of 1,211,977.73 yuan. Credit included: Interest on deposits in banks 407,273.71 yuan, investment income 831,534.76 yuan, handling fee income 82,867.81 yuan, and miscellaneous profit and loss 55,074.89 yuan, totaling 1,376,751.17 yuan. At the end of the statement, it was sealed and certified by accountant Xie Lin.

No Increase in Shareholders

After the meeting, according to General Manager Song Ziliang's statement to the Central News Agency reporter, the report that the company would increase its capital by 50 million yuan was inaccurate. The establishment of a real estate mortgage bank was only due to instructions from the Ministry of Finance to draft measures, which are currently being prepared for submission to the Ministry of Finance for approval to establish the bank. However, the bank has no relationship with China Construction Bank Corporation and will be independently established by the Ministry of Finance. Whether its capital will be allocated by the government or jointly operated by attracting merchant shares has not yet been determined, but it is heard that bonds will be issued to supplement the capital.

Exchange Method

The reporter of Xinsheng News Agency interviewed Secretary-General Lin of the Banking Association yesterday. According to him, the issue of banks exchanging unified public bonds for bonds held in custody or mortgage has been submitted to the executive committee of the association for approval. The method of exchange by banks on behalf of customers will be announced by the association. The method is roughly the same as that of the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications. The methods of the two banks are recorded as follows: 1. For the convenience of those entrusting the bank for custody, all bonds in custody will be exchanged for new bonds by the bank on their behalf. 2. Those entrusting the bank for custody who do not need to entrust the bank for exchange but want to exchange on their own must notify the bank before March 5. If they do not notify within the time limit, they will be deemed to have entrusted the bank for exchange and will be handled in accordance with the first article. 3. If the balance of the remaining principal of each type of old bond is less than 10 yuan, it should be calculated at 98% in national currency to make up 10 yuan. 4. The bank's previous bond custody receipt should be exchanged for a new public bond custody receipt at the bank two weeks after the exchange date specified by the Ministry of Finance for various bonds. The original seal must be brought for verification when exchanging the receipt. In the future, principal and interest will be collected with the new custody receipt. 5. If customers who entrust the bank do not come to exchange for the new custody receipt after the deadline, the names of the bonds listed on the old custody receipt will be invalid. The bank will store the new public bonds to be exchanged in accordance with the regulations of the Ministry of Finance. Because these new public bonds are subject to lottery, it is hoped that they will come to the bank to exchange for new custody receipts as soon as possible to avoid losing the right to the new public bond lottery. Please pay special attention.

Reduced Imports of Foreign Rice, Shanghai Rice Merchants Mostly Unprepared to Order from Overseas, Expected to Decrease by at Least One-Third This Year 101

Regarding the production and sales of rice, government officials and grain merchants have been striving to improve the situation in recent years, in order to stop the leakage of foreign rice imports every year. A reporter from the Central News Agency interviewed a prominent grain merchant yesterday, who said that since last year, imports of foreign rice have decreased compared to previous years. The autumn harvest in various rice-producing areas last year was still abundant, and the government has continued to pay close attention to grain storage this year. Since the beginning of this year, although the poor economic situation has prevented large households from absorbing and hoarding, and rice prices have not been strong, rice is still a necessity, and the average annual sales volume has not fluctuated much. Because there is no shortage of rice produced last year, rice merchants in Shanghai, based on the situation in previous years, would have rushed to order foreign rice from foreign merchants in order to sell it at a profit. However, this year, rice merchants have not made any preparations for this. In addition to ordering a very small amount of broken rice from Siam, they have not taken any action on rice from places such as Saigon and Rangoon. Therefore, it is expected that imports of foreign rice will decrease by at least one-third this year.

Chinese Tea, Packaging Needs Urgent Improvement, British Government Plans to Prohibit Imports, Foreign Firms Greatly Alarmed 102

Since the overproduction and plummeting prices of tea in the world, tea merchants in India, Ceylon, the Dutch East Indies, and other countries have implemented export restriction agreements. The export quantity of Indian and Dutch tea has decreased, and the market price has slightly recovered. However, the export of low-grade black tea from China and Japan has increased. For example, the export of black tea from Hunan and Hubei in China has increased significantly compared to before 1932. This is because the selling price is indeed cheaper than Indian and Dutch tea of the same grade. The effectiveness of the export restriction agreements of Indian and Dutch tea merchants has inevitably been greatly affected. Recently, there have been rumors in the London tea market citing the poor packaging of Chinese tea boxes. The purpose of this is self-evident. However, in order to protect the industry of its colonies, the British government has been incited and may issue an order prohibiting the import of substandard tea boxes at any time. Therefore, British merchants engaged in the export of Chinese tea are generally alarmed. Mr. Lacklan, a well-known tea technician at the London headquarters of Jardine Matheson, sent a long letter to Shanghai, urging them to quickly take necessary measures to avoid unexpected losses. The manager of Jardine Matheson's Shanghai office immediately wrote to the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau, asking them to find ways to improve the packaging of Chinese tea boxes, and the language was extremely sincere. It is said that the bureau has paid close attention to the inspection of tea box packaging. Before the start of the tea season last year, it had already published a notice in the newspaper, urging tea merchants in the interior to actively improve. This year, it has revised three articles of the tea box crackdown measures with the Hankou Commodity Inspection Bureau, including: 1. Four wooden strips must be added to each of the four corners and upper and lower edges inside the box, a total of twelve strips, to increase the support of the tea box. 2. Clean paper must be used on the inner wall of the lead foil to properly paste it, so that the tea leaves and the lead foil are completely isolated. 3. The type of tea, trademark, (main items) number of pieces, gross weight, and net weight (new system), time of picking and making, tea plantation number, and location must be noted on the outside of the box. Once approved by the Ministry of Industry, it can be strictly implemented after the new tea is on the market. In addition, the bureau, in order to sympathize with the difficulties of merchants, has also issued a notice to all export tea merchants to cooperate jointly. In order to encourage tea merchants in the interior to improve automatically, all old regulations on "packaging" and "repairing boxes" must be waived for those who can improve the tea box packaging in accordance with the above methods. At the same time, after the tea boxes are strengthened, leaks and shortages of weight can be reduced, and the aroma and quality will not be reduced. If the old-fashioned and inferior packaging from the past is still used, it must be repackaged before it can be exported, and all repackaging costs must be borne by the original manufacturer. After the reporter went to the bureau to inspect the new and sturdy improved tea boxes, the degree of firmness seemed to be indeed different from the old-fashioned tea boxes. Moreover, only twelve more wooden strips need to be nailed during the improvement, which costs very little and is indeed an essential plan for improving tea at present. The bureau has taken clear photos for reference by tea merchants in remote areas. It is said that tea merchants send letters to the bureau to request them for imitation almost every day.

Kunming Plane Forced to Land, China National Aviation Corporation Receives Telegram on Whereabouts, Fuselage and Engine Destroyed, Pilot, Electrician, and Passengers All Safe 103

On the 5th of this month, the China National Aviation Corporation's three-engine Chongqing-Kunming-Qian-Kunming "Kunming" plane arrived in Guiyang that day.
